The breed is prone to spinal problems, especially intervertebral disk disease (IVDD), due in part to an extremely long spinal column and short rib cage. As with every dog breed, the exact breeding history and development of physical characteristics is unknown, but the flap-down ears and famous curved tail of the have deliberately said to be bred into the dog. In the case of the ears, this is to keep grass seeds, dirt, and other matter from entering the ear canal. The curved tail is dual-purposed: to be seen more easily in long grass and, in the case of burrowing Xs, to help haul the dog out if it becomes stuck in a burrow. ↵ ID X

(Asked gpt to help me frame the following, because I was struggling to articulate it well): ↵  _An intriguing part at the beginning of Jared Diamond’s Guns, Germs, and Steel highlights the contrast between Papua New Guinea, Indonesia, and the Polynesian countries (Hawaii, Samoa, etc). All of these regions began with similar conditions: numerous indigenous languages, small-scale societies, and long geographic separation from other advanced civilizations._ ↵ _Yet their historical trajectories diverged dramatically. In Polynesia, the development of extraordinarily effective seafaring* enabled long-distance settlement, sustained inter-island contact, and the spread of a relatively unified language and culture across vast oceanic distances. By contrast, Papua New Guinea and much of Indonesia remained highly fragmented. Their rugged mountains, dense forests, and scattered islands limited both movement and large-scale integration. This fragmentation was compounded by their *north–south orientation* , which spans sharply different climates and ecological zones over short distances, making the transfer of crops, animals, and technological innovations extremely difficult. Polynesia, by contrast, benefited from more consistent climates along the islands they colonized, and their seafaring networks reinforced integration rather than isolation. Diamond’s comparison illustrates how geography, climate orientation, and technological innovation together shape patterns of settlement, societal structure, and the astonishing diversity of human languages and cultures._ ↵ *interestingly, many centuries before Europeans achieved intercontinental travel... Had to bring this up to get a Portuguese colleague to pipe down when he was being pompous about how they first managed to crack long-distance travel by sea
